  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b2be2caf-aba1-46e1-b69e-378e4a9ef6a0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText11204995428660783203" style="display:none">In the city of Atlanta, women are dying—at the hands of a killer who signs his work with a single, chilling act of mutilation. Leaving behind enough evidence to fuel a frenzied police hunt, this cunning madman is bringing together dozens of lives, crossing the boundaries of wealth and race. And the people who are chasing him must cross those boundaries too. Among them is Michael Ormewood, a veteran detective whose marriage is hanging by a thread—and whose arrogance and explosive temper are threatening his career. And Angie Polaski, a beautiful vice cop who was once Michael's lover before she became his enemy.<br /><br />But another player has entered the game: a loser ex-con who has stumbled upon the killer's trail in the most coincidental of ways—someone who may be the key to breaking the case wide open...</span>

<div id="review_2108575389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2108575389" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2108575389?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1432792988789613837"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>The beginning of this book was absolutely brilliant. It's hard to explain without ruining it for someone who hasn't read it yet, but the way Slaughter set the tone and your beliefs regarding certain characters and then turned them on their heads was seriously awesome. I have never read a book where the author managed that in quite that way. <br/><br/>This was my first Karin Slaughter book. It was excellently written and the story very layered. It stalled a little bit for me toward the middle mark</span>
  <span id="freeText1432792988789613837" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br>The beginning of this book was absolutely brilliant. It's hard to explain without ruining it for someone who hasn't read it yet, but the way Slaughter set the tone and your beliefs regarding certain characters and then turned them on their heads was seriously awesome. I have never read a book where the author managed that in quite that way. <br><br>This was my first Karin Slaughter book. It was excellently written and the story very layered. It stalled a little bit for me toward the middle mark (thus my rating) but I still enjoyed it a lot. <br><br>Will is a VERY interesting character. So was Angie, although I spent the majority of the book wanting to punch her upside her damned head. She and Will are damaged with a capital "D." I'm curious to see where this series and their story goes, so I will definitely be checking out the next one. <br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer11238275829918700012">Triptych. <br/>A three panel painting or photograph. Generally a large center panel with a hinged smaller panel on either side. <br/>The three panels combined may display one larger view, three different views of the same subject or three related subjects. <br/>The casual observation will enjoy the three panel experience. <br/>Intellectual observers will contemplate weather the three views together offer a larger spectrum of it's subject. <br/>It's the curious observer that sees the hinges..... <br/></span>

<div id="review_3383472183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3383472183" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3383472183?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36311231-triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3383472183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9418107771594523408"><i>“Three canvases hinged together to make one image when it was open, another image when it was closed.”</i><br/><br/><b>Three perspectives. Three different versions of the same event. When brought together they paint a picture of one sick, sadistic, and dangerous individual. </b><br/><br/>When a homicide detective is called to the scene of a brutal murder, he reflects on his own life. A newly released convicted sex offender and murderer struggles to assimilate. A vice cop is haunted by her past. All three perspectives are put </span>
  <span id="freeText9418107771594523408" style="display:none"><i>“Three canvases hinged together to make one image when it was open, another image when it was closed.”</i><br /><br /><b>Three perspectives. Three different versions of the same event. When brought together they paint a picture of one sick, sadistic, and dangerous individual. </b><br /><br />When a homicide detective is called to the scene of a brutal murder, he reflects on his own life. A newly released convicted sex offender and murderer struggles to assimilate. A vice cop is haunted by her past. All three perspectives are put together by Will Trent revealing an entirely different point of view on a serial killer who is about to strike one last time.<br /><br />The narrative is divided into three main parts: Part I is narrated by Detective Michael Ormewood. Part II by John Shelley and Part III is split between Will Trent and Angie Polaski. It’s not until 40% in that the reader is introduced to Will POV. I was expecting Will to have a bigger voice, but he stays quietly in the background until it’s time to strike. <br /><br />I started this series by reading book number 8, so I was familiar with Will and Angie’s characters. However, reading this first installment made me regret starting this series in the middle, as I went into this book with some preconceived notions about Angie and Will. It was interesting to view their relationship in a different light. <br /><br />Triptych is a gruesome and dark thriller that I could not put down. Similar to other Slaughter books, some scenes are extremely difficult to read due to their disturbing nature. She does not hold back when it comes to sharing sick and twisted details. <b>This book is not for the faint of heart.</b><br /> <br />Each part concludes with a huge reveal that had me taken by surprise.<b> The first major twist I didn’t see coming and had me shaking my head (in a good way) at how skillfully Slaughter pulls this off and makes me want to read everything she has ever written! I have only read two books in this series and I am already addicted. I will be planning a Will Trent binge-fest soon! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9418107771594523408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3404270409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3404270409" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3404270409?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/25786785-triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3404270409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13158023568941023200">I will start by saying that Karin Slaughter is a pretty darn good thriller writer<br/><br/>I will follow that by saying she goes to some pretty dark and disturbing places. I almost feel bad enjoying her stories as much as I do! But that is the thing with a good escape, it often takes you places you may not normally be comfortable going. You know . . . pushing the limits can be quite a ride!<br/><br/>With Triptych, Slaughter starts a new series with protagonist Will Trent. He is a very interesting character that I a</span>
  <span id="freeText13158023568941023200" style="display:none">I will start by saying that Karin Slaughter is a pretty darn good thriller writer<br /><br />I will follow that by saying she goes to some pretty dark and disturbing places. I almost feel bad enjoying her stories as much as I do! But that is the thing with a good escape, it often takes you places you may not normally be comfortable going. You know . . . pushing the limits can be quite a ride!<br /><br />With Triptych, Slaughter starts a new series with protagonist Will Trent. He is a very interesting character that I am glad to know I am not done with yet. He was fleshed out so well that I want to know more and see him in action. And, in addition to Will being an interesting character – all the characters from this book are wonderfully flawed. Whether their flaws make them tragic heroes or twisted maniacs, they are all fun to read about. I love the way she introduces each of them and then fills the reader in with their back stories (one backstory went on for so long, I started to forget about the main story – but that was just fine!). And, none of the characters are plain vanilla or cookie cutter – all are unique – like nothing I have read before.<br /><br />Back to my comment about pushing the limits. I love her writing and her books, but Slaughter always goes almost too far with her plot devices. Some readers may be put off by this. So, if you do not like your crime novels gory and your sexual situations kind of twisted, this may not be the book for you. But I will say that even though she gets pretty extreme, it always feels like it fits. I don’t get this feeling like she forced a scenario in for shock value. That, to me, is a sign of a great writer.<br /><br />If you give it a shot, I think you will be enthralled. But, don’t say I didn’t warn you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13158023568941023200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1399348533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399348533" />
    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399348533?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399348533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16698040789683506733">This was another first for me. It was my first crime thriller and my first book by Karin Slaughter. Is <b>Triptych</b> a book I would have picked out for myself? Probably not but that is the beauty of Goodreads. <br/><br/>For the last few weeks I have been following by sweet friend Mo’s status updates and review’s for this series and kept toying with the thought of picking this one up and jumping into the series. I worried that it would be too shocking and hideous, a story that wouldn’t appeal to me. There were </span>
  <span id="freeText16698040789683506733" style="display:none">This was another first for me. It was my first crime thriller and my first book by Karin Slaughter. Is <b>Triptych</b> a book I would have picked out for myself? Probably not but that is the beauty of Goodreads. <br><br>For the last few weeks I have been following by sweet friend Mo’s status updates and review’s for this series and kept toying with the thought of picking this one up and jumping into the series. I worried that it would be too shocking and hideous, a story that wouldn’t appeal to me. There were moments that were rather shocking and hideous but I quickly found myself unable to turn away from the story, the mystery and the characters. I am hooked. I will be making my way through this series. <br> <br>There is a peculiarity about Will Trent that has me intrigued. I need to know more about this guy and <b>Triptych</b> is just the beginning.<br><br>The setting is Atlanta, Georgia. When the book starts out we are hit with a gruesome murder of a hooker. The writing of the scene was so vivid and shocking. The platform had been set. A few characters had been introduced and the mystery begins. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Triptych/47f552cd-e459-4fae-ace0-f0c427b560db_zpsxmepj4o6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443581491i/16380790._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 47f552cd-e459-4fae-ace0-f0c427b560db_zpsxmepj4o6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As each character is introduced and their personal stories start to unfold I struggled with keeping my emotions and reaction towards them in check. With the investigation of the most recent murder underway, there are certain things that link it to past attacks and murders. We are introduced to a character John Shelley whose life was stripped away from him at a young age, convicted of one of these past murders. He is finally given his freedom back only to be faced with the fear of someone toying with that freedom. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Triptych/30be8a61-d286-4f85-9133-57f31260364f_zps7rnjcoge.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443581491i/16380791.jpg" alt=" photo 30be8a61-d286-4f85-9133-57f31260364f_zps7rnjcoge.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When the Atlanta police department sets out to find the person who committed this horrid crime different angles are pursued and nothing is clear cut. Michael Ormewood was the lead investigator and was rather combative at every turn but he had earned his rank and he would do his job. He is paired with Leo, an older detective and he was that buffer and the one that smoothed out Michael’s wrinkles.<br><br>But there was some crazy shit going on. People had been murdered, a young girl has gone missing and there was some guy out there that has to be stopped. The pieces of the puzzle were not coming together quick enough. He had to be found.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Triptych/64b2abbf-9423-40a4-bb98-05a65f58d9e6_zpsxop3feok.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443581491i/16380792._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 64b2abbf-9423-40a4-bb98-05a65f58d9e6_zpsxop3feok.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Angie Polaski was a vice cop who was also working the case. She was someone difficult to figure out. She was rough, lived life hard and did her job well. She shared a past with two men and was engaging in a relationship with another man. This was typical of Angie. She was like a Triptych. A canvas that appeared one way on the outside but different on the inside. Her life was about to implode.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Triptych/ae3afafb-9841-498a-b208-2a59dc1f9a6d_zpsmrumanra.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443581491i/16380793.jpg" alt=" photo ae3afafb-9841-498a-b208-2a59dc1f9a6d_zpsmrumanra.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tangled within this mystery is the man that has me intrigued. <b>Will Trent.</b> <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/Triptych/6f4cfc44-4f1c-4eac-b9ff-6942f3664098_zps2m6ii6gf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443581491i/16380794.jpg" alt=" photo 6f4cfc44-4f1c-4eac-b9ff-6942f3664098_zps2m6ii6gf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Early on in the story we learn of his past, his relationships and his affliction. His determination and his inquisitiveness is what sets him aside as a Special Agent. It also gets him into trouble. Will has this sixth sense with things and decides to check into a lead that starts to put the pieces of the puzzle together. But a moment of doubt sets a certain ball rolling. Will has to rely on someone he didn't expected to. In the end it was a choice that made all the difference.<br><br>This one was a definite winner for me. I’ve already started Fractured. Loving it so far!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16698040789683506733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1648670069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648670069" />
    <a title="Miriam Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35740838-miriam-smith"><img alt="Miriam Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534659500p2/35740838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648670069?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miriam Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miriam Smith" href="/user/show/35740838-miriam-smith">Miriam Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781844138562" href="/book/show/2283543.Triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648670069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13891478240063036282">Wow!!!! I only wish I could give this book "Triptych" 6 stars as in my opinion this is one hell of a story and definitely my type of book! <br/>This is a no holes barred book that is gritty, gruesome, highly addictive and an absolute page turner that I totally devoured in a couple of days. If you are particularly offended by vicious violence or the world of seedy prostitution then this book may not be for you but I thought Karin captured it all perfectly, especially John's time in prison which I was </span>
  <span id="freeText13891478240063036282" style="display:none">Wow!!!! I only wish I could give this book "Triptych" 6 stars as in my opinion this is one hell of a story and definitely my type of book! <br />This is a no holes barred book that is gritty, gruesome, highly addictive and an absolute page turner that I totally devoured in a couple of days. If you are particularly offended by vicious violence or the world of seedy prostitution then this book may not be for you but I thought Karin captured it all perfectly, especially John's time in prison which I was utterly moved by and truly felt his torment. <br />I loved the way Karin described the areas in the book, I really felt like I was there with the characters and appreciate that Karin has put a lot into relating this to the reader. It's difficult to say much about the story without giving away spoilers but there are some clever twists and turns in a very carefully planned plot that concludes in an intense shocking climax between killer and victim and is just outstanding. <br />I've had this book on my bookshelf for a few years now not realising it featured Special Agent Will Trent and only wish I'd read it sooner as it's a brilliant book introducing Will and his history. Although this is a standalone book it can be read with or without further Will Trent books. <br />Karin Slaughter has always been and always will be one of my favourite authors, her writing is so professional, polished and she certainly knows how to pack a punch. A must read that I highly recommend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13891478240063036282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_460303904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460303904" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460303904?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460303904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16500509503933966322">Triptych by Karin Slaughter is a 2006 Delacorte Press publication. <br/><br/> I have read other books by this author, but somehow, I never got around to the Will Trent series. With a new installment slated for release this month, I decided to try playing catch up, which shouldn’t be too hard with only seven more to read after this one. <br/> <br/><br/>So, first up is Triptych, originally published in 2006. This story introduces us to Will Trent, a Georgia Bureau of Investigation specialist, who arrives in Atlanta after </span>
  <span id="freeText16500509503933966322" style="display:none">Triptych by Karin Slaughter is a 2006 Delacorte Press publication. <br /><br /> I have read other books by this author, but somehow, I never got around to the Will Trent series. With a new installment slated for release this month, I decided to try playing catch up, which shouldn’t be too hard with only seven more to read after this one. <br /> <br /><br />So, first up is Triptych, originally published in 2006. This story introduces us to Will Trent, a Georgia Bureau of Investigation specialist, who arrives in Atlanta after a string of murders involving teenage girls, catches his attention.<br /> The case reunites Will with his best friend during childhood, and former lover, Angie Polanski, a vice cop, with a plethora of intimacy issues, that constantly drives the couple apart. <br /><br />As Will and Angie navigate the treacherous waters of race and wealth, amid the troublesome rumors surrounding one of the officers close to case, they unwittingly discover a link from the past involving the murder of another teenager. The connection they uncover is explosive, but soon becomes a matter of life and death, when another girl goes missing. <br /><br />Well, I certainly understand why this series is so well received. The author does an amazing job of developing the characters, building suspense, and adding in uncomfortable issues that might make you squirm a little. These issues add layers of conflict and controversy to the already complicated murder investigation. <br /><br />The beginning of the book can be a little uneven at times because the set up involves the introduction of several storylines, and timelines, going on all at once. But, it’s not long before the threads begin to connect and it all starts to make sense. Somewhere around the midway mark, I became immersed in the story so completely, I didn’t want to move, not even for a bathroom break. <br /><br />The story is dark, graphic, gritty and disturbing, but also challenging and thought provoking and is just the type of thriller I enjoy most. <br /><br />Overall this first book in the series has roped me in and waiting impatiently in line at the library for the next book in the series. <br /><br />4 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16500509503933966322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16764595758872077398"><b> EDIT: Reread as of December 1, 2015</b><br/><br/>Sometimes, if I'm in a good mood, I believe in second chances. That's why we have rehab because some people need to have another shot. <br/><br/>I decided to give <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_' title='Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Triptych</a> another chance because <b> Hridya</b> said that Michael (the fucktard who I thought was the lead) is not the hero of this book but Will Trent. I should have known this obvious fact because Will Trent's name is the also the name for this series. Sometimes my stupidity astounds me.<br/><br/>Anyway, so there I was, rerea</span>
  <span id="freeText16764595758872077398" style="display:none"><b> EDIT: Reread as of December 1, 2015</b><br><br>Sometimes, if I'm in a good mood, I believe in second chances. That's why we have rehab because some people need to have another shot. <br><br>I decided to give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_" title="Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Triptych</a> another chance because <b> Hridya</b> said that Michael (the fucktard who I thought was the lead) is not the hero of this book but Will Trent. I should have known this obvious fact because Will Trent's name is the also the name for this series. Sometimes my stupidity astounds me.<br><br>Anyway, so there I was, rereading this book and here are my thoughts.<br><br><b>The Good</b><br><br>The gore. My goodness the gorey scenes in this book is amazing. I love my crime books dirty and gritty and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> gave that to me so kudos to that.<br><br><i> The character: John Shelley</i><br><br>I actually feel sorry for this dude. He's the type of character that needs to have a second chance. I was horrified with what he experienced inside the prison and I love the way he stood up with himself in the end.<br><br><i> The character: Will Trent</i><br><br>Because.<br><br><br><b> The Bad</b><br><br>Maybe I'm not that sold to this book because I found out who's the motherfucking bastard in this story. I was already half way in the book when I realized who's chopping the tongues of those teenagers and lemme tell you, that took the thrill out of the book.<br><br>I also find the out of order flashbacks of John Shelley's life annoying. I think the author did that to make it interesting but it didn't work for me. It only add confusion and I was like meh.<br><br><br><b> The Evil</b><br><br>The characters. All of these fucktards are in my shit list.<br><br>Let me start with Angie- <br><br>First of all bitch, I don't like you. How can I when you're an ungrateful twat who loves to hurt those around you. You use people like a discarded tissue and I never liked how you use Will like he's your fuckboy or something.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448966448ra/17215193.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Michael</b><br><br>Of all the motherfuckers, you are the motherfuckest. Fuck you too.<br><br><br>******<br>I do not like infidelity (who the fuck does?) that's why when I found out that our wonderful hero has an affair with a 15 year old girl, I stopped reading immediately. Don't try to change my mind, trolls .That's just gross.I'll be reading more of Karin Slaughter's works in the future but for now..<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445296505ra/16625575.gif" width="268" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445296505ra/16625576.gif" width="268" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445296505ra/16625577.gif" width="268" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445296505ra/16625578.gif" width="268" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445296505ra/16625579.gif" width="268" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1414021424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1414021424" />
    <a title="Krystin Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15477771-krystin-rachel"><img alt="Krystin Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172064p2/15477771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1414021424?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystin Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystin Rachel" href="/user/show/15477771-krystin-rachel">Krystin Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=just-one-more-chapter">just-one-more-chapter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=serial-killers">serial-killers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=fbi">fbi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=procedural">procedural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=desert-island-picks">desert-island-picks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=series-book-one">series-book-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15477771-krystin-rachel?shelf=challenge-2016">challenge-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414021424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2620717098444776575">If anything ever called for a Space Jam gif it's this review.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471731973ra/20100184.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ummmm, so yeah I liked this. <b>Like, a lot.</b> <br/><br/>I'm not drooling all over myself like I did for <i>Pretty Girls</i> (the first Karin Slaughter novel I'd ever read, excuse me, I'm so sorry) but I'm definitely feeling like a Serbian who just won a gold medal for water polo at the summer Olympics. And I know how this might feel because that's exactly what I'm watching while I type this. And let me tell you, they are definitely excited men in a pool. S</span>
  <span id="freeText2620717098444776575" style="display:none">If anything ever called for a Space Jam gif it's this review.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471731973ra/20100184.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ummmm, so yeah I liked this. <b>Like, a lot.</b> <br><br>I'm not drooling all over myself like I did for <i>Pretty Girls</i> (the first Karin Slaughter novel I'd ever read, excuse me, I'm so sorry) but I'm definitely feeling like a Serbian who just won a gold medal for water polo at the summer Olympics. And I know how this might feel because that's exactly what I'm watching while I type this. And let me tell you, they are definitely excited men in a pool. So that's what I am - an excited Serbian in pool. Side note: how much do you want to bet those skull hats are what's causing so many of them to go bald?<br><br>But I digress...somehow in my long and illustrious mystery-thriller reading <s>definitely not a career</s> career I had totally missed out on Will Trent and this series. Until now. Who knows what took me so long. Maybe it was college. Maybe it was Netflix. Maybe it was some other shiny words bound together. Maybe I'm just an asshole (likely.) But now that I'm here I'm going to stick around and make my ass comfortable on this bandwagon. <br><br>Karin Slaughter is turning into one of my favourite authors. <b>I find her characters to be so robust</b>, so interesting. Her plotting is exceptional, setting up each connecting story line with ease and without giving anything away. I mean she even throws in small, delightful ties about something as simple as how a dog came to be named Betty. <b>I just enjoy reading her stories so much.</b> <br><br>And <i>Triptych</i> is just another confirmation of this.<br><br>The story introducing Will Trent and Angie Polaski, revolving around Michael Ormewood, John Shelley, a 20 year old murder, recent serial murders, protitutes and the Atlanta streets is just a masterful example of mystery writing. Plotting, red herrings, character development, setting, history...it's just:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471731973ra/20100185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Being the first in a series, there was a lot of set up for the first quarter of the book, and while mostly necessary, I did find some of it dragged a little bit. But once I got in the heart of it, I was hooked. I had to pee so badly at one point, but I didn't dare put the book down and walk away. Was potential bladder damage and the danger of wetting the bed next to my husband worth it? <b>I'm going to have to say yes, yes it was.</b><br><br>Just like my first foray with Karin Slaughter thanks to <i>Pretty Girls</i>, I once again come away from my reading adventure with hearts in my eyes. <b><i>Triptych</i> was a gritty and complex mystery.</b> But most importantly (to me), it seemed honest and walked the line of being graphic, unflinching, and unapologetic about it's darkness without being overwrought or excessive. I was sucked into this world and never questioned the story's probability. <br><br>Loved it. Loved the characters. <b>Loved loved LOVED</b> Will Trent. Would totally do Angie. Will definitely be in for the second novel. 4.5 stars.<br><br>You got me Karin Slaughter. You got me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471731973ra/20100186.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2620717098444776575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372485151" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18335294606543040990">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>A bit gruesome at times but a solid read. Will Trent is a very intriguing character. And the people who are chasing him must cross those boundaries too</i></b></blockquote></span>

And Angie Polaski, a beautiful vice cop who was once Michael's lover before she became his enemy.<br><br>But another player has entered the game: a loser ex-con who has stumbled upon the killer's trail in the most coincidental of ways—someone who may be the key to breaking the case wide open</i>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=black-as-mitchell-s-heart">black-as-mitchell-s-heart</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842015118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11061830389499979425">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Holy poop I’m really far behind on reviewing. And you know what’s awesome? All the library books I read while on Christmas vacay are now disappearing from my Kindle making my notes go “poof” . . . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580556.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>(Hey Goodreads, why don’t you figure out how to make your super not awesome feature of Kindle note sharing work for library books instead of just shit I had to buy on Amazon. Kthanks!)<br/><br/>Anyway, like I said I’m really far behind, I read </span>
  <span id="freeText11061830389499979425" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Holy poop I’m really far behind on reviewing. And you know what’s awesome? All the library books I read while on Christmas vacay are now disappearing from my Kindle making my notes go “poof” . . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580556.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>(Hey Goodreads, why don’t you figure out how to make your super not awesome feature of Kindle note sharing work for library books instead of just shit I had to buy on Amazon. Kthanks!)<br><br>Anyway, like I said I’m really far behind, I read this nearly two weeks ago and I am senile so I don’t have any quotey quotes to share. You’ll just have to trust me that the dialogue on this was pretty decent and there were some quotables. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96699019?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelby</a> (Ha! I totally got to link one of your “I lurved it, it was gud” reviews LOLOLOLOL) has been telling me to read Karen Slaughter until she’s blue in the face, but I’m a jerkoff so I ignored her. (Really I was a little terrified I would hate it and then she would cut me.) Good news is, I didn’t hate it at all. And to Karen Slaughter . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580557.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>At the risk of sounding sexist against my own fairer sex, I never cease to be amazed by women authors who are willing to take things to an uncomfortable level with zero shits given. Caroline Kepnes did it with an anti-hero you just couldn’t stop yourself from falling in love with, Ania Ahlborn does it with horror and Karen Slaughter does it with crime fiction. <br><br>The story here is about dead women in Atlanta whose murders may be connected. “May” being the operative word due to the fact that they don’t fit the typical serial killer scenario since they are of different ages and socioeconomic backgrounds. They all have something in common, however, that is a potential link – their tongues have been bitten off. Makes you hungry, right????<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580558.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Detective Michael Ormewood has been assigned the latest case when a fella named Will Trent enters the scene offering to help. Then things get a little cray and you get to find out just how intricate a spider web Karen Slaughter is capable of weaving together.<br><br>So like I said, I’m officially a Karen Slaughter fangirl now. I had my doubts after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372492569?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Girls</a>, but I’m going to trust Shelby and say that one was just a fluke. Now, Slaughter does have her moments and this was <s>a real Stephen King</s> in need of leaving some pages on the cutting room floor, but other than those times where I was screaming . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580559.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was a solid start to a series.<br><br>Things I loved (aside from the stabby stabby):<br><br>1. Will Trent. J.K. Rowling did it with Cormoran Strike and Karen Slaughter did it with Will Trent. Instead of some super hot supersleuth, Will kind of resembles this guy . . . .<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wait, that’s not right. He really kinda looks like this . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580561.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>He’s not pretty. He’s also seriously effing broken and you’ll totally fall in love with him (if you’re smart it will be a not-sexy way because Shelby called dibs a long time ago). <br><br>2. Speaking of broken, meet the female lead in this series Angie Polaski. As a future Rock ‘N Roll Hall of Fame inductee once said . . . .<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580562.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>“She’s a crazy bitch.”<br><br>It’s A-Okay to have this type of reaction to her too . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483116509ra/21580563.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She’s seriously punchable and also a little awesome.<br><br>3. The change in perspective. I didn’t expect the narrator to change and it threw me for a loop for a bit, but boy was that a good idea.<br><br>4. Knowing the “whodunit” early. I love a good mystery that confirms your suspicions early and allows you to sit back and enjoy the ride while the characters play catch up.<br><br>If you’re a fan of crime thrillers, this is an author to definitely check out. <br><br></span>

<div id="review_2004587907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004587907" />
    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004587907?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099481836" href="/book/show/1433150.Triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004587907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7969401890779665407">Things moved a bit slowly in the first few chapters that I almost lost my interest in them several times. Fortunately, after the 20% mark, the pace picked up and around halfway through the story, I found myself drawn into this murder investigation in such a way that I had a hard time putting it down. But sadly, there was something I didn't like in the latter part of the book which sort of ruined my enjoyment from the previous chapters.<br/><br/>I must admit I had high hopes for this series as I've heard m</span>
  <span id="freeText7969401890779665407" style="display:none">Things moved a bit slowly in the first few chapters that I almost lost my interest in them several times. Fortunately, after the 20% mark, the pace picked up and around halfway through the story, I found myself drawn into this murder investigation in such a way that I had a hard time putting it down. But sadly, there was something I didn't like in the latter part of the book which sort of ruined my enjoyment from the previous chapters.<br /><br />I must admit I had high hopes for this series as I've heard many good things about it. But I'm sad to report that Triptych couldn't be considered a total success for me. It was, in fact, not that the plot was bad per se, but it’s just that I've already read something way better, creepier, scarier, crueler, more chilling, and more gripping than this one before.<br /><br />There was nothing new about the plot. The mystery aspect was predictable that I saw it coming a mile away. I could also easily identify the killer even before I reached the second half. And that was a bit too boring for me!<br /><br />I don't understand why the title of this series has to be 'Will Trent'. I think the proper one should be 'Angie Polaski series' instead since she literally stole every scene she appeared in. Wasn't Will supposed to be the star of this book? Wasn’t he supposed to be the cleverest person or the clearest thinker in this story? I expected a lot from him, but he turned out to be the least important character here. Let’s just say, he wasn’t as smart as I initially thought he would be. If you ask me, he was overshadowed by almost every other character; damn, even John could make more brilliant decision than him!<br /><br />Honestly, I couldn't care less about Will. He was just too weak for my liking.<br /><br />Anyway, let’s talk about Angie since I found that she was the most interesting and complex character in this book. She seemed tough, invincible, cold, and sometimes bitchy on the outside, but soft, scarred, and vulnerable on the inside. In my opinion, Angie was the real highlight of this book. I loved how she managed to remain cool and collected in the most life-threatening crisis and got out of it on her own. (Sorry Will, but you weren’t needed here.)<br /><br />Well, to tell you the truth, despite the predictable plot and my problem with Will’s character, there were multiple things I enjoyed about this book. And you know what? Just when I was ready to give 4 stars to it, then Will messed things up by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[arresting John <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I wasn’t impressed with how he handled the whole situation after that. It wasn’t the smartest move at all.<br /><br />And when I finished reading this, I asked myself “Did the good outweigh the bad?” I’m still not sure of an answer to this question. The book was neither great nor awful. All I could say is that it wasn’t an outstanding read in comparison to the other books I’ve read in the same genre.<br /><br />Overall, this was a somewhat lackluster mystery/thriller story. Nothing special about the plot to remember. I partially enjoyed it nevertheless.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7969401890779665407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580244647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2039245595148025993">3 "gruesome, page turning, don't know when to stop" stars !!!<br/><br/> This is my first Slaughter novel and I have to say that I feel pretty mixed about it.<br/> <br/> Aspects of this book were really excellent. Ms. Slaughter has a way of building up a story to a harsh crescendo with many interesting and somewhat believable characters that collide in a very dysfunctional and bloody mess. I could not help but continue this book despite the very intense violence and hopelessness that permeates much of this narrative</span>
  <span id="freeText2039245595148025993" style="display:none">3 "gruesome, page turning, don't know when to stop" stars !!!<br /><br /> This is my first Slaughter novel and I have to say that I feel pretty mixed about it.<br /> <br /> Aspects of this book were really excellent. Ms. Slaughter has a way of building up a story to a harsh crescendo with many interesting and somewhat believable characters that collide in a very dysfunctional and bloody mess. I could not help but continue this book despite the very intense violence and hopelessness that permeates much of this narrative. There is a lot of torture and gruesomeness here and is not for the squeamish or faint of heart. Despite this the story is extremely fascinating and I just had to find out how all the pieces would come together in the end.<br /><br /> Triptych is a novel that with a more careful and thoughtful hand could have ended up being a noir detective masterpiece instead of a pretty good police thriller. Ms. Slaughter starts off by knitting an intricate cable knit sweater but often forgets the stitch, switches shades of yarn or in some cases even leaves some areas incomplete.<br /><br /> I will add book 2 to my TBR queue and hope that she takes these very interesting and damaged characters and places them in a story that is less sensationalist and more focused on consistency and logical conclusions.<br /><br />Here is a little clip of the author speaking about this book:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bm-csseMDqQ">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bm-cs...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2039245595148025993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001921921" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001921921?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12859870-triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001921921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3939921200702892796">This is the first in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter' title='Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karin Slaughter</a>'s Will Trent series and the first book I've read of hers. We are introduced to Will Trent, a Special Georgia Bureau of Investigation agent, called in to help local police with difficult crimes. Will is a loner and a damaged man, having been abused as a child, his 6'4" body covered in scars. He met his best friend and sometime lover Angie in a State orphanage and she is the only person he lets get close to him. Angie is tough as nails, currently an undercover </span>
  <span id="freeText3939921200702892796" style="display:none">This is the first in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a>'s Will Trent series and the first book I've read of hers. We are introduced to Will Trent, a Special Georgia Bureau of Investigation agent, called in to help local police with difficult crimes. Will is a loner and a damaged man, having been abused as a child, his 6'4" body covered in scars. He met his best friend and sometime lover Angie in a State orphanage and she is the only person he lets get close to him. Angie is tough as nails, currently an undercover policewoman in Vice dressing as a prostitute to arrest men soliciting on the streets. <br /><br />Will arrives in Atlanta following the brutal death of a woman who is left mutilated and choking to death on her own blood. The mutilation of her body is similar to that of two young girls attacked elsewhere and Will believes a serial rapist is at large and may have escalated to murder. At around the time of the first attack, John Shelley was released from prison after 23y for rape and murder of a 15y old girl. John just wants to put his time in prison behind him and get on with rebuilding his life but someone has other plans for him.<br /><br />This was quite a graphic and gripping novel with plenty of nail biting action as Will hunts down the rapist and killer. I look forward to reading more in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3939921200702892796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2069227147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2069227147" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2069227147?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099481836" href="/book/show/1433150.Triptych">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror">mystery-thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=trigger-warning">trigger-warning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069227147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786657471479467065"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501006436i/23407588._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Book 2</u> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071620939' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fractured</a></b> ★★★1/2<br/><b><u>Book 3</u> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072732512' rel='nofollow noopener'>Genesis/Undone</a></b> ★<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501014957i/23408747._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've said it before, but the <i>whodunits</i> and what not aren't what compel me to read thrillers, but rather <b>the unflinching look they take at the most gruesome and disgusting parts of our human world.</b> I've guessed who the killer was in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_' title='Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie & Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkness, Take My Hand</a> halfway through it, and it remains one of my favorite thriller, because sometimes, the characterization, the <i>Hows</i> and <i>Whens</i> and <i>Whys</i> are just so much more important and interesting than the big r</span>
  <span id="freeText8786657471479467065" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501006436i/23407588._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Book 2</u> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071620939" rel="nofollow noopener">Fractured</a></b> ★★★1/2<br><b><u>Book 3</u> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072732512" rel="nofollow noopener">Genesis/Undone</a></b> ★<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501014957i/23408747._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've said it before, but the <i>whodunits</i> and what not aren't what compel me to read thrillers, but rather <b>the unflinching look they take at the most gruesome and disgusting parts of our human world.</b> I've guessed who the killer was in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21681.Darkness__Take_My_Hand__Kenzie___Gennaro___2_" title="Darkness, Take My Hand (Kenzie &amp; Gennaro, #2) by Dennis Lehane" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness, Take My Hand</a> halfway through it, and it remains one of my favorite thriller, because sometimes, the characterization, the <i>Hows</i> and <i>Whens</i> and <i>Whys</i> are just so much more important and interesting than the big reveal. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501014957i/23408748._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_" title="Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Triptych</a> is one of these books.</b> Even though I've known - <i>known</i> - in my core who the psychopath was for more than 200 pages, I couldn't look away until the very end. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> puts so much care in her characters - villains included - that even though you want them to burn, you don't want them to get caught in some two-pages scene and call it a day : you want closure, and she delivers. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501014957i/23408749._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm going to warn you : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_" title="Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Triptych</a> is short on likeable characters, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> doesn't shy away from picturing <b>gruesome violence on page,</b> so perhaps don't read it if that's something that could trigger you. The story being told through multiple - and unreliable - narrators, I can assure you that you'll want OUT of several of these minds. I've been feeling on the edge of vomiting from page one, and Will's chapters were the only ones that could bring a tiny smile on my face. Will, whose name prevented me from stopping my read when I realized - thanks to the series' name and friends' reviews - that <i>he</i> was meant to be the hero, and not that fucker of Michael Ormewood. Will, whom I wanted to protect from the moment I met him, probably because of his dyslexia and the way people - and himself - treated him. As a teacher, I've seen too often how self-depreciation can go hands in hands with learning disorders, and it breaks my heart every damned time. Oh, and probably because he's the only character who's thoroughly likeable and did I say that you'll want to protect him? Yeah? <br><br>In the end, I feel sick to my stomach but I can't deny that I don't regret starting this series for one second : thrillers whose appeal doesn't revolve around some final twist are way too rare for me to look away, and I'll definitely read more of Will Trent's investigations really soon. <b>Recommended.</b><br><br><b>TW - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape, attempted rape, pedophilia, graphic violence, ableist, homophobic, sexist and racist slurs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1055932131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055932131" />
    <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf"><img alt="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540171256p2/9185509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055932131?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf">Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055932131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12049277386965414129">3.5 rounded up<br/><br/>I got a copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49975863.The_Silent_Wife__Will_Trent___10_' title='The Silent Wife (Will Trent, #10) by Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Silent Wife</a> from the lovely peeps over at Harper Collins Australia. Soon I realised that it was number 10 in the Will Trent series. I am a bit reluctant to read it because I hate going into series after the characters have been established. So I read some reviews and it seems people RAVE about this series! And other works by Karin Slaughter. So I thought, why not give number 1 in the series a go and see if i can get through a few of them before I tackle number 1</span>
  <span id="freeText12049277386965414129" style="display:none">3.5 rounded up<br /><br />I got a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49975863.The_Silent_Wife__Will_Trent___10_" title="The Silent Wife (Will Trent, #10) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silent Wife</a> from the lovely peeps over at Harper Collins Australia. Soon I realised that it was number 10 in the Will Trent series. I am a bit reluctant to read it because I hate going into series after the characters have been established. So I read some reviews and it seems people RAVE about this series! And other works by Karin Slaughter. So I thought, why not give number 1 in the series a go and see if i can get through a few of them before I tackle number 10!<br /><br />This one was exciting, not because I loved it, which unfortunately I did not -but it introduced me to her clever writing. There is so much talent there, and so much potential. I loved how it was written. She weaved the story together really well and everything came together and it was really well done.<br /><br />The characters, I’m not so fussed about right now to be honest. I am not Angie’s biggest fan, and her relationship with Will is weird and I just didn’t feel it. I am imagining that this improves over subsequent books, because of all the amazing reviews this series gets. At least I hope it does!<br /><br />I really enjoyed how the killer was revealed, it was done in such a way that it wasn’t a twist exactly, but there were still surprises.<br /><br />The audio version was good, I would have preferred to read this one in print I think, but due to a bunch of other books I have to get through, audio it was. And it was relatively short and easy to listen to.<br /><br />I am anticipating good things with this series, hope I am not disappointed!<br /><br /><i>I purchased Triptych at my own expense on audible.com.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12049277386965414129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Across town John Shelley just released from prison after serving 20 years for rape and murder, has problems of his own, a dead end job, and that everyone knows that he served time for killing a 15 year old girl.<br /><br />Though there are mysteries along the way, how did John manage to compile a great credit rating and whats the connection between the violence past and present?<br /><br />The heroes and villains, who act both surprisingly and logically are a welcome sign that Slaughter's great work only hints at her talent of her gifts. <br /><br />This book is definitely not for the faint at heart.   <span id="freeText1918692594158340017" style="display:none">This, Triptych, is as close to man-fiction as a book written by a woman can get. But gosh, was it good?!!<br /><br />I cried, I laughed, I gasped in surprise countless times. The story was totally engrossing. Karin Slaughter definitely knows what she's doing. But don't read it if graphic violence makes you cringe. Don't read it if you want to believe all inmates are the scum of the earth. Don't read it if you have manly bits and are particularly sensitive, I can't guarantee there won't be trauma. And if you do decide to read it, and you did read plenty of K. Slaughter already, know this: the first half of the book rocks! But after a major twist and revelation (you'll know when you come to it) our dear writer falls back onto her old patterns. Not that it makes a bad book. Quite the contrary. But the first half led me into thinking that this would be The Crime Masterpiece. Triptych being merely a damn good thriller? That's just unbearable, but that's what it was. Evil book! Evil Karin Slaughter, how dare she teasing me like that. <br /><br /></span>
