<div id="review_419982307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419982307" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419982307?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419982307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1375002485017099295">Will Trent, an agent for the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, is teamed with Atlanta detective Michael Ormewood to investigate a series of brutal crimes in which someone is killing women and cutting out their tongues. <br/><br/>Everyone in the book is damaged in some way. Oremwood has a troubled marriage and a child who is mentally challenged. Trent, who is severely dyslexic, had a very troubled childhood. His best friend, Angie Polaski, is a vice cop with a troubled past of her own. Added to the mix is J</span>
  <span id="freeText1375002485017099295" style="display:none">Will Trent, an agent for the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, is teamed with Atlanta detective Michael Ormewood to investigate a series of brutal crimes in which someone is killing women and cutting out their tongues. <br /><br />Everyone in the book is damaged in some way. Oremwood has a troubled marriage and a child who is mentally challenged. Trent, who is severely dyslexic, had a very troubled childhood. His best friend, Angie Polaski, is a vice cop with a troubled past of her own. Added to the mix is John Shelly, recently released from prison after being convicted of murdering a girl when he was only a teenager. Coincidentally, her tongue was bitten off as well.<br /><br />The book alternates between the cops' view and that of John Shelly, and it has a very split personality. The scenes from Shelly's view are vivid and engaging and bring home in a very realistic way the horrors of prison and the way in which a parolee is totally at the mercy of the system. Any misstep can send him back to a cell. The scenes from the cops' point of view seem dull and plodding by comparison, and it was hard to work up much enthusiasm for any of those characters.<br /><br />Shelly insists that he was innocent of the crime for which he was convicted, and he fears that someone is attempting to frame him for the current murders and send him back to prison. There are a number of twists and turns that amp up the suspense a bit, but this could have benefitted from being a tighter, leaner book with more appealing characters among the cops.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1375002485017099295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review419982307">

They elicit all the feels and I need more of Will Trent (and Angie!) in my life! <br/><br/><b>My favorite quote:</b><br/><i>“It didn't take a Harvard economist to figure out that it'd be a hell of a lot cheaper spending money on helping keep kids safe when they were yo</i></span>

That was the American way, though. Spend a million dollars rescuing some kid who's fallen down a well, but God forbid you spend a hundred bucks up front to cap the well so the kid never falls down it in the first place.”</i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663852100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10434099624581694558">Women are being killed in Atlanta. Their killings are similar but how are they related. How are the characters in this book related.<br/><br/>There appears at times to be various story lines going on in this book. <br/><br/>In one a teenager, John, is accused of murdering the girl he has feelings for. He is tried as an adult and is sent to prison. He is brutally attacked and tormented losing appeal after appeal. Finally, his time is up and he is on parole, trying to make a life for himself but he soon learns someon</span>
  <span id="freeText10434099624581694558" style="display:none">Women are being killed in Atlanta. Their killings are similar but how are they related. How are the characters in this book related.<br /><br />There appears at times to be various story lines going on in this book. <br /><br />In one a teenager, John, is accused of murdering the girl he has feelings for. He is tried as an adult and is sent to prison. He is brutally attacked and tormented losing appeal after appeal. Finally, his time is up and he is on parole, trying to make a life for himself but he soon learns someone has stolen his identity and may be trying to destroy his life.<br /><br />In another a detective, Michael, who is married with a child who is developmentally disabled. He is working the case to figure out who the killer of the women is. He comes off likable at first but soon, his polished demeanor begins to fade.<br /><br />In another, Will Trent, is called in to assist local police (including Michael) solve the case. Will Trent is a mystery. We know he had a sad past full of abuse and that he grew up in foster care. He is reunited with Angie, a female detective working undercover, who he met when he was 8 in foster care.<br /><br />Angie is the piece that ties them altogether. Their stories brilliantly fit together as Will investigates the recent murder of a prostitute. <br /><br />This was a very enjoyable read.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10434099624581694558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15551949927902132901"><b>3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Don't click on spoilers unless you've read the story before because it will ruin the mystery. The spoilers are a few things that didn't make sense to me.</b><br/><br/>I really liked the story, but I wish Will was in it more, especially in the beginning. I'm already rooting for this underdog-type detective. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I will say Ms. Slaughter did completely make me think Michael was a good guy at first, and even felt sorry for him!   <span id="freeText15551949927902132901" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars<br /><br />Don't click on spoilers unless you've read the story before because it will ruin the mystery. The spoilers are a few things that didn't make sense to me.</b><br /><br />I really liked the story, but I wish Will was in it more, especially in the beginning. I'm already rooting for this underdog-type detective. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I will say Ms. Slaughter did completely make me think Michael was a good guy at first, and even felt sorry for him! What a complete psycho! He didn't suffer nearly as much as I wished! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The chapters changing going back and forth in years made it so it took me a bit to get into the story. I can't believe that John Shelley wouldn't have <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[said something about his cousin to someone over the years. Also, Will let Michael go and question Jasmine alone when he had doubts about him?! And the fact she goes missing right after doesn't make Will immediately think of Michael since he had just questioned her? I don't know, but that didn't make sense to me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As for Angie, wish I liked her more because she clearly has had a rough time, but I can see she's not good for Will. She may or may not love him, but she treats him like crap. Unfortunately, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I hear she isn't going away anytime soon.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Love the idea of Will having a tiny Chihuahua dog he can't help but spoil. <br /><br />I will be continuing with book two soon. :)<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7943114841716940900" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me on Goodreads by Bips sometime ago and for whatever reasons I have continually put it to one side while I read another book.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rZMl7MjnZ22iesrUoP8KXd10EUFHLBXglhi2rMeCMD7+R9hepP6221ec26FnFA6BoeO5PY5C8djk3nAv7KNmiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2GX8IBq5C3tWe/IJwoipksYtez8fBdebSQjrJ4+RtOCLsQGSdqDazaOd43wFY61OurrTQ9ZrM6M7zi2kpLDiVw==')})
  }
//]]>

And when Rowan Caine arrives at Heatherbrae House, she is smitten—by the luxurious “smart” home fitted out with all modern conveniences, by the beautiful Scottish Highlands, and by this picture-perfect family. What she doesn’t know is that she’s stepping into a nightmare—one that will end with a child dead and herself in prison awaiting trial for murder. Writing to her lawyer from prison, she struggles to explain the unravelling events that led to her incarceration. It wasn’t just the constant surveillance from the cameras installed around the house, or the malfunctioning technology that woke the household with booming music, or turned the lights off at the worst possible time. It wasn’t just the girls, who turned out to be a far cry from the immaculately behaved model children she met at her interview. It wasn’t even the way she was left alone for weeks at a time, with no adults around apart from the enigmatic handyman, Jack Grant. It was everything. She knows she’s made mistakes. She admits that she lied to obtain the post, and that her behavior toward the children wasn’t always ideal. She’s not innocent, by any means. But, she maintains, she’s not guilty—at least not of murder. Which means someone else is. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7629345107871532310">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAS</span>
  <span id="freeText7629345107871532310" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAST WIDOW, features Sara Linton and Will Trent. Slaughter is the founder of the Save the Libraries project—a nonprofit organization established to support libraries and library programming. A native of Georgia, Karin Slaughter lives in Atlanta. Her standalone novels PIECES OF HER, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and COP TOWN are in development for film and television.<br /><br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter">Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter</a> <br /><br /><b>Website</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.karinslaughter.com/">http://www.karinslaughter.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/karinslaughterauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/karinslaugh...</a><br /></span>
